        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Local authorities in Namibia can be in the form of municipalities (either Part 1 or Part 2 municipalities), town councils or villages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alan_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-alan-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:left;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Namibia" title="Economy of Namibia">
        Economy of Namibia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Windhoek,_Independence_Avenue.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="1000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg/220px-Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg/330px-Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg/440px-Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Windhoek,_Independence_Avenue.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Downtown
         <a href="/wiki/Windhoek" title="Windhoek">
          Windhoek
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG/220px-Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG/330px-Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG/440px-Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Tsumeb" title="Tsumeb">
          Tsumeb
         </a>
         's main road
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Namibia's economy is tied closely to South Africa's due to their shared history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Intelligence1_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Intelligence1-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Department1_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Department1-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The largest economic sectors are mining (10.4% of the gross domestic product in 2009), agriculture (5.0%), manufacturing (13.5%), and tourism.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usds_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-usds-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Namibia has a highly developed banking sector with modern infrastructure, such as online banking and cellphone banking. The Bank of Namibia (BoN) is the central bank of Namibia responsible for performing all other functions ordinarily performed by a central bank. There are 5 BoN authorised commercial banks in Namibia: Bank Windhoek, First National Bank, Nedbank, Standard Bank and Small and Medium Enterprises Bank.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the Namibia Labour Force Survey Report 2012, conducted by the
       <a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Namibia_Statistics_Agency" title="de:Namibia Statistics Agency">
        Namibia Statistics Agency
       </a>
       , the country's unemployment rate is 27.4%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       "Strict unemployment" (people actively seeking a full-time job) stood at 20.2% in 2000, 21.9% in 2004 and spiraled to 29.4% in 2008. Under a broader definition (including people that have given up searching for employment) unemployment rose to 36.7% in 2004. This estimate considers people in the
       <a href="/wiki/Informal_sector" title="Informal sector">
        informal economy
       </a>
       as employed. Labour and Social Welfare Minister
       <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Ngatjizeko" title="Immanuel Ngatjizeko">
        Immanuel Ngatjizeko
       </a>
       praised the 2008 study as "by far superior in scope and quality to any that has been available previously",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but its methodology has also received criticism.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2004 a labour act was passed to protect people from job discrimination stemming from pregnancy and HIV/AIDS status. In early 2010 the Government
       <a href="/wiki/Tender_board" title="Tender board">
        tender board
       </a>
       announced that "henceforth 100 per cent of all unskilled and semi-skilled labour must be sourced, without exception, from within Namibia".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2013, global business and financial news provider,
       <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">
        Bloomberg
       </a>
       , named Namibia the top emerging market economy in Africa and the 13th best in the world. Only four African countries made the Top 20 Emerging Markets list in the March 2013 issue of Bloomberg Markets magazine, and Namibia was rated ahead of
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       (19th), South Africa (15th) and
       <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">
        Zambia
       </a>
       (14th). Worldwide, Namibia also fared better than Hungary, Brazil and Mexico. Bloomberg Markets magazine ranked the top 20 based on more than a dozen criteria. The data came from Bloomberg's own financial-market statistics, IMF forecasts and the World Bank. The countries were also rated on areas of particular interest to foreign investors: the ease of doing business, the perceived level of corruption and economic freedom. In order to attract foreign investment, the government has made improvement in reducing red tape resulted from excessive government regulations making the country one of the least bureaucratic places to do business in the region. However, facilitation payments are occasionally demanded by customs due to cumbersome and costly customs procedures.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Namibia is also classified as an Upper Middle Income country by the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
        World Bank
       </a>
       , and ranks 87th out of 185 economies in terms of ease of doing business.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_living_in_Namibia" title="Cost of living in Namibia">
        cost of living in Namibia
       </a>
       is relatively high because most of the goods including cereals need to be imported. Business monopoly in some sectors causes higher profit bookings and further raising of prices.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Its capital city, Windhoek is currently ranked as the 150th most expensive place in the world for expatriates to live.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_Namibia" title="Taxation in Namibia">
        Taxation in Namibia
       </a>
       includes personal income tax, which is applicable to total taxable income of an individual and all individuals are taxed at progressive marginal rates over a series of income brackets. The value added tax (VAT) is applicable to most of the commodities and services.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay,_2005.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg/220px-Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg/330px-Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg/440px-Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay%2C_2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sandstorm_while_driving_from_Swakopmund_to_Walfish_Bay,_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/B2_road_(Namibia)" title="B2 road (Namibia)">
          B2
         </a>
         between
         <a href="/wiki/Swakopmund" title="Swakopmund">
          Swakopmund
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">
          Walvis Bay
         </a>
         , Namibia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Despite the remote nature of much of the country, Namibia has seaports, airports, highways, and
       <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Namibia" title="Rail transport in Namibia">
        railways
       </a>
       (narrow-gauge). The country seeks to become a regional transportation hub; it has an important seaport and several landlocked neighbours. The Central Plateau already serves as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation_corridor" title="Transportation corridor">
        transportation corridor
       </a>
       from the more densely populated north to South Africa, the source of four-fifths of Namibia's imports.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Almanac_2004_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-World_Almanac_2004-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">
        Agriculture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Agriculture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Namibia" title="Agriculture in Namibia">
        Agriculture in Namibia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schildburgsdorf.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="167" data-file-width="326" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Schildburgsdorf.jpg/220px-Schildburgsdorf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Schildburgsdorf.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schildburgsdorf.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Welcoming sign of the
         <i>
          Burgsdorf
         </i>
         farm in
         <a href="/wiki/Hardap_Region" title="Hardap Region">
          Hardap
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       About half of the population depends on agriculture (largely
       <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">
        subsistence agriculture
       </a>
       ) for its livelihood, but Namibia must still import some of its food. Although per capita GDP is five times the per capita GDP of Africa's poorest countries, the majority of Namibia's people live in rural areas and exist on a subsistence way of life. Namibia has one of the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">
        highest rates of income inequality
       </a>
       in the world, due in part to the fact that there is an urban economy and a more rural cash-less economy. The inequality figures thus take into account people who do not actually rely on the formal economy for their survival. Although arable land accounts for only 1% of Namibia, nearly half of the population is employed in agriculture.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Almanac_2004_88-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-World_Almanac_2004-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       About 4,000, mostly white, commercial farmers own almost half of Namibia's arable land.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The governments of Germany and Britain will finance Namibia's
       <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">
        land reform
       </a>
       process, as Namibia plans to start expropriating land from white farmers to resettle landless black Namibians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Agreement has been reached on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privatisation" title="Privatisation">
        privatisation
       </a>
       of several more enterprises in coming years, with hopes that this will stimulate much needed foreign investment. However, reinvestment of environmentally derived capital has hobbled Namibian per capita income.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lange_91-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lange-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of the fastest growing areas of economic development in Namibia is the growth of
       <a href="/wiki/Communal_Wildlife_Conservancies_in_Namibia" title="Communal Wildlife Conservancies in Namibia">
        wildlife conservancies
       </a>
       . These conservancies are particularly important to the rural, generally unemployed, population.
      </p>
      <p>
       An
       <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">
        aquifer
       </a>
       called "Ohangwena II" has been discovered, capable of supplying the 800,000 people in the North for 400 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aqui_92-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aqui-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Experts estimate that Namibia has 7,720 km
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       of underground water.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afr_93-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-afr-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aqmap_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aqmap-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mining_and_electricity">
        Mining and electricity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mining and electricity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Namibia" title="Mining in Namibia">
        Mining in Namibia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Providing 25% of Namibia's revenue, mining is the single most important contributor to the economy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Namibia is the fourth largest exporter of non-fuel minerals in Africa and the world's fourth largest producer of
       <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">
        uranium
       </a>
       . There has been significant investment in
       <a href="/wiki/Uranium_mining" title="Uranium mining">
        uranium mining
       </a>
       and Namibia is set to become the largest exporter of uranium by 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rich
       <a href="/wiki/Alluvium" title="Alluvium">
        alluvial
       </a>
       diamond deposits make Namibia a primary source for gem-quality diamonds.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While Namibia is known predominantly for its gem diamond and uranium deposits, a number of other minerals are extracted industrially such as
       <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">
        lead
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">
        tungsten
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">
        gold
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">
        tin
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluorspar" title="Fluorspar">
        fluorspar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">
        manganese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">
        marble
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">
        copper
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">
        zinc
       </a>
       . There are offshore gas deposits in the Atlantic Ocean that are planned to be extracted in the future.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usds_78-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-usds-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to "The Diamond Investigation", a book about the global diamond market, from 1978,
       <a href="/wiki/De_Beers" title="De Beers">
        De Beers
       </a>
       , the largest diamond company, bought most of the Namibian diamonds, and would continue to do so, because "whatever government eventually comes to power they will need this revenue to survive".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Domestic supply voltage is 220V AC. Electricity is generated mainly by thermal and hydroelectric power plants. Non-conventional methods of electricity generation also play some role. Encouraged by the rich uranium deposits the Namibian government plans to erect its first nuclear power station by 2018, also uranium enrichment is envisaged to happen locally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saveorsink_99-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Saveorsink-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Equus_burchelli_4.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2056" data-file-width="2742" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Equus_burchelli_4.jpg/220px-Equus_burchelli_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Equus_burchelli_4.jpg/330px-Equus_burchelli_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Equus_burchelli_4.jpg/440px-Equus_burchelli_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Equus_burchelli_4.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An example of Namibian wildlife, the
         <a href="/wiki/Plains_zebra" title="Plains zebra">
          plains zebra
         </a>
         , is one focus of tourism.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Namibia" title="Tourism in Namibia">
        Tourism in Namibia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Tourism is a major contributor (14.5%) to Namibia's GDP, creating tens of thousands of jobs (18.2% of all employment) directly or indirectly and servicing over a million tourists per year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country is a prime destination in Africa and is known for
       <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">
        ecotourism
       </a>
       which features
       <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Namibia" title="Wildlife of Namibia">
        Namibia's extensive wildlife
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goodshape_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-goodshape-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There are many lodges and reserves to accommodate eco-tourists. Sport hunting is also a large, and growing component of the Namibian economy, accounting for 14% of total tourism in the year 2000, or $19.6 million US dollars, with Namibia boasting numerous species sought after by international sport hunters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humavindu_102-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Humavindu-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, extreme sports such as
       <a href="/wiki/Sandboarding" title="Sandboarding">
        sandboarding
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skydiving" title="Skydiving">
        skydiving
       </a>
       and 4x4ing have become popular, and many cities have companies that provide tours.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The most visited places include the capital city of
       <a href="/wiki/Windhoek" title="Windhoek">
        Windhoek
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">
        Caprivi Strip
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fish_River_Canyon" title="Fish River Canyon">
        Fish River Canyon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sossusvlei" title="Sossusvlei">
        Sossusvlei
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Skeleton_Coast" title="Skeleton Coast">
        Skeleton Coast
       </a>
       Park,
       <a href="/wiki/Sesriem" title="Sesriem">
        Sesriem
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Etosha_Pan" title="Etosha Pan">
        Etosha Pan
       </a>
       and the coastal towns of
       <a href="/wiki/Swakopmund" title="Swakopmund">
        Swakopmund
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">
        Walvis Bay
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCderitz" title="Lüderitz">
        Lüderitz
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The capital city of Windhoek plays a very important role in Namibia's tourism due to its central location and close proximity to
       <a href="/wiki/Hosea_Kutako_International_Airport" title="Hosea Kutako International Airport">
        Hosea Kutako International Airport
       </a>
       . According to The Namibia Tourism Exit Survey, which was produced by the
       <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Challenge_Corporation" title="Millennium Challenge Corporation">
        Millennium Challenge Corporation
       </a>
       for the Namibian Directorate of Tourism, 56% of all tourists visiting Namibia during the time period, 2012 – 2013, visited Windhoek.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many of Namibia's tourism related parastatals and governing bodies such as Namibia Wildlife Resorts,
       <a href="/wiki/Air_Namibia" title="Air Namibia">
        Air Namibia
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Namibia_Tourism_Board" title="Namibia Tourism Board">
        Namibia Tourism Board
       </a>
       as well as Namibia's tourism related
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_association" title="Trade association">
        trade associations
       </a>
       such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Hospitality_Association_of_Namibia" title="Hospitality Association of Namibia">
        Hospitality Association of Namibia
       </a>
       are also all headquartered in Windhoek.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also a number of notable hotels in Windhoek such as
       <a href="/wiki/Windhoek_Country_Club_Resort" title="Windhoek Country Club Resort">
        Windhoek Country Club Resort
       </a>
       and some international hotel chains also operate in Windhoek, such as Avani Hotels and Resorts and
       <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Hilton Hotels &amp; Resorts">
        Hilton Hotels and Resorts
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Namibia's primary tourism related governing body, the
       <a href="/wiki/Namibia_Tourism_Board" title="Namibia Tourism Board">
        Namibia Tourism Board
       </a>
       (NTB), was established by an Act of Parliament: the Namibia Tourism Board Act, 2000 (Act 21 of 2000). Its primary objectives are to regulate the tourism industry and to market Namibia as a tourist destination.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also a number of
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_association" title="Trade association">
        trade associations
       </a>
       that represent the tourism sector in Namibia, such as the Federation of Namibia Tourism Associations (the umbrella body for all tourism associations in Namibia), the
       <a href="/wiki/Hospitality_Association_of_Namibia" title="Hospitality Association of Namibia">
        Hospitality Association of Namibia
       </a>
       , the Association of Namibian Travel Agents, Car Rental Association of Namibia and the Tour and Safari Association of Namibia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">
        Water supply and sanitation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Namibia" title="Water supply and sanitation in Namibia">
        Water supply and sanitation in Namibia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Namibia is the only country in Sub-Saharan Africa to provide water through municipal departments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_108-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The only bulk water supplier in Namibia is
       <a href="/wiki/NamWater" title="NamWater">
        NamWater
       </a>
       , which sells it to the respective municipalities which in turn deliver it through their reticulation networks.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_108-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In rural areas, the Directorate of Rural Water Supply in the Ministry of Agriculture, Water and Forestry is in charge of drinking water supply.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_108-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        UN
       </a>
       evaluated in 2011 that Namibia has improved its water access network significantly since independence in 1990. A large part of the population can not, however, make use of these resources due to the prohibitively high consumption cost and the long distance between residences and water points in rural areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_108-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result, many Namibians prefer the traditional wells over the available water points far away.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_109-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Compared to the efforts made to improve access to safe water, Namibia is lagging behind in the provision of adequate sanitation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This includes 298 schools that have no toilet facilities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Over 50% of child deaths are related to lack of water, sanitation, or hygiene; 23% are due to diarrhea alone. The UN has identified a "sanitation crisis" in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_109-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Apart from residences for upper and middle class households, sanitation is insufficient in most residential areas. Private flush toilets are too expensive for virtually all residents in
       <a href="/wiki/Township" title="Township">
        townships
       </a>
       due to their water consumption and installation cost. As a result, access to
       <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">
        improved sanitation
       </a>
       has not increased much since independence: In Namibia's rural areas 13% of the population had more than basic sanitation, up from 8% in 1990. Many of Namibia's inhabitants have to resort to "flying toilets", plastic bags to defecate which after use are flung into the bush.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The use of open areas close to residential land to urinate and defecate is very common
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and has been identified as a major
       <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Namibia" title="Health in Namibia">
        health hazard
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_111-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Namibia" title="Demographics of Namibia">
        Demographics of Namibia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Population_Density_(2011).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="836" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg/220px-Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg/330px-Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg/440px-Namibia_Population_Density_%282011%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Population_Density_(2011).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Population density in Namibia by regions (census 2011)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Namibia has the second-
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" title="List of countries by population density">
        lowest population density
       </a>
       of any sovereign country, after
       <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">
        Mongolia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unpop_114-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unpop-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The majority of the Namibian population is of
       <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">
        Bantu
       </a>
       -speaking origin – mostly of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ovambo_people" title="Ovambo people">
        Ovambo
       </a>
       ethnicity, which forms about half of the population – residing mainly in the north of the country, although many are now resident in towns throughout Namibia. Other ethnic groups are the
       <a href="/wiki/Herero_people" title="Herero people">
        Herero
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Himba_people" title="Himba people">
        Himba people
       </a>
       , who speak a similar language, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Damara_(people)" title="Damara (people)">
        Damara
       </a>
       , who speak the same "click" language as the
       <a href="/wiki/Nama_people" title="Nama people">
        Nama
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to the Bantu majority, there are large groups of
       <a href="/wiki/Khoisan" title="Khoisan">
        Khoisan
       </a>
       (such as Nama and
       <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">
        San
       </a>
       ), who are descendants of the original inhabitants of Southern Africa. The country also contains some
       <a href="/wiki/Angolans_in_Namibia" title="Angolans in Namibia">
        descendants of refugees from Angola
       </a>
       . There are also two smaller groups of people with mixed racial origins, called "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coloured_People_in_Namibia" title="Coloured People in Namibia">
        Coloureds
       </a>
       " and "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basters" title="Basters">
        Basters
       </a>
       ", who together make up 8.0% (with the Coloureds outnumbering the Basters two to one). There is a substantial
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Namibia" title="Chinese people in Namibia">
        Chinese minority in Namibia
       </a>
       ; it stood at 40,000 in 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG/220px-Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG/330px-Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG/440px-Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Himba_Woman_and_Family.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Himba_people" title="Himba people">
          Himba people
         </a>
         in northern Namibia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_African" title="White African">
        Whites
       </a>
       (mainly of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrikaner_people" title="Afrikaner people">
        Afrikaner
       </a>
       , German, British and
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       origin) make up between 4.0 and 7.0% of the population. Although their percentage of population is decreasing due to
       <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">
        emigration
       </a>
       and lower birth rates they still form the second-largest population of
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">
        European ancestry
       </a>
       , both in terms of percentage and actual numbers, in
       <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">
        Sub-Saharan Africa
       </a>
       (after South Africa).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_116-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The majority of
       <a href="/wiki/White_Namibians" title="White Namibians">
        Namibian whites
       </a>
       and nearly all those who are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basters" title="Basters">
        mixed race
       </a>
       speak
       <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">
        Afrikaans
       </a>
       and share similar origins, culture, and religion as the white and coloured populations of South Africa. A large minority of whites (around 30,000) trace their family origins back to the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Namibians" title="German Namibians">
        German
       </a>
       settlers who colonized Namibia prior to the British confiscation of German lands after World War One, and they maintain German cultural and educational institutions. Nearly all Portuguese settlers came to the country from the former
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_West_Africa" title="Portuguese West Africa">
        Portuguese colony
       </a>
       of Angola.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The 1960 census reported 526,004 persons in what was then South-West Africa, including 73,464 whites (14%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Children_in_Namibia(1_cropped).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1003" data-file-width="1353" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg/220px-Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg/330px-Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg/440px-Children_in_Namibia%281_cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Children_in_Namibia(1_cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Children in Namibia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Namibia conducts a census every ten years. After
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independence_of_Namibia" title="Independence of Namibia">
        independence
       </a>
       the first Population and Housing Census was carried out in 1991; further rounds followed in 2001 and 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001Census_119-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2001Census-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The data collection method is to count every person resident in Namibia on the census reference night, wherever they happen to be. This is called the
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       method.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For enumeration purposes the country is demarcated into 4,042
       <i>
        enumeration areas
       </i>
       . These areas do not overlap with constituency boundaries to get reliable data for election purposes as well.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 2011 Population and Housing Census counted 2,113,077 inhabitants of Namibia. Between 2001 and 2011 the annual population growth was 1.4%, down from 2.6% in the previous ten–year period.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snapshot_122-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-snapshot-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Namibia" title="Religion in Namibia">
        Religion in Namibia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3684" data-file-width="5526" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg/220px-Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg/330px-Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg/440px-Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Swakopmund_ev-luth_Kirche_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Lutheran church in
         <a href="/wiki/Swakopmund" title="Swakopmund">
          Swakopmund
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Christian community makes up 80%–90% of the population of Namibia, with at least 75% being
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
        Protestant
       </a>
       , and at least 50%
       <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">
        Lutheran
       </a>
       . Lutherans are the largest religious group – a legacy of the German and
       <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">
        Finnish
       </a>
       missionary work during the country's colonial times. 10%–20% of the population hold
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">
        indigenous
       </a>
       beliefs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_116-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Missionary activities during the second half of the 19th century resulted in many Namibians converting to Christianity. Today most Christians are Lutheran, but there also are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">
        Roman Catholic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">
        Methodist
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">
        Anglican
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/African_Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="African Methodist Episcopal Church">
        African Methodist Episcopal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">
        Dutch Reformed
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">
        Mormons
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
        The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Namibia" title="Islam in Namibia">
        Islam in Namibia
       </a>
       is subscribed to by about 9,000 Muslims,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       many of whom are Nama.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Namibia is home to a small
       <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
        Jewish
       </a>
       community of about 100 members.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary1_125-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary1-125">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
        Language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Namibia" title="Languages of Namibia">
        Languages of Namibia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="914" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg/220px-NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg/330px-NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg/440px-NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NamibiaMehrsprachigkeit.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Although its official language is English, Namibia is a multilingual country as is illustrated by these examples in English, German,
         <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">
          Afrikaans
         </a>
         and
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oshiwambo_language" title="Oshiwambo language">
          Oshiwambo
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Up to 1990, English,
       <a href="/wiki/German_language_in_Namibia" title="German language in Namibia">
        German
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">
        Afrikaans
       </a>
       were official languages. Long before Namibia's independence from South Africa, SWAPO was of the opinion that the country should become officially monolingual, choosing this approach in contrast to that of its neighbour South Africa (which granted
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Africa" title="Languages of South Africa">
        all 11 of its major languages
       </a>
       official status), which was seen by them as "a deliberate policy of ethnolinguistic fragmentation."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Consequently, SWAPO instituted English as the sole official language of Namibia though only about 3% of the population speaks it as a home language. Its implementation is focused on the civil service, education and the broadcasting system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kriger_127-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-kriger-127">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some other languages have received semi-official recognition by being allowed as medium of instruction in primary schools. It is expected of private schools to follow the same policy as state schools, and "English language" is a compulsory subject.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kriger_127-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-kriger-127">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As in other postcolonial African societies, the push for monolingual instruction and policy has resulted in a high rate of school drop-outs and of individuals whose academic competence in any language is low.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the 2011 census, the most common languages are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oshiwambo" title="Oshiwambo">
        Oshiwambo
       </a>
       (the most spoken language for 49% of households),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nama_language" title="Nama language">
        Nama
       </a>
       /
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Damara_language" title="Damara language">
        Damara
       </a>
       (11.3%), Afrikaans (10.4%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kavango_languages" title="Kavango languages">
        Kavango
       </a>
       (9%),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otjiherero" title="Otjiherero">
        Otjiherero
       </a>
       (9%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snapshot_122-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-snapshot-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census2011_130-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-census2011-130">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most widely understood and spoken language is
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       . Both Afrikaans and English are used primarily as a second language reserved for public communication.
      </p>
      <p>
       Most of the white population speaks either German or Afrikaans. Even today, 103 years after the end of the German colonial era, the German language plays a role as a commercial language. Afrikaans is spoken by 60% of the white community, German is spoken by 32%, English is spoken by 7% and Portuguese by 1%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_116-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Geographical proximity to Portuguese-speaking Angola explains the relatively high number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_speaker" title="Portuguese speaker">
        Portuguese speakers
       </a>
       ; in 2011 these were estimated to be 100,000, or 4–5% of the total population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
        <a href="#cite_note-131">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>

       </span>
      </h3>

       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">
         7
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:left;">
         <a href="/wiki/Katima_Mulilo" title="Katima Mulilo">

         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:left;">
         <a href="/wiki/Zambezi_Region" title="Zambezi Region">
          Zambezi
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:right;">
         28,362
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">

        </td>

        </td>
